وفي مثال الخادم الذي ذكرته لك آنفاً ما ينبهك إلى هذه الحقيقة . فقد قلنا : إنك لم ترد إطلاق يده بالتصرف بمالك كما يشاء ، إلا وأنت مريد لظهور نتيجة ذلك أياً كانت النتيجة سواء كنت تحبها وترضاها أم لا .. وهذه حقيقة نلمسها جميعاً في تجاربنا وتصرفاتنا الشخصية ومعاملة بعضنا لبعض ، إنني بكل تأكيد ، لا أحب من تلميذي أن يكون مخفقاً في دراسته غير ناجح فيها ، وأظل أكرر على مسامعه الأمر بالدراسة وبذل الجهد ، ومع ذلك فأنا عندما أريد أن أختبره في نهاية العام، فإن إرادتي تسري من غير شك إلى النتيجة التي سيكشف عنها ذلك الاختيار ، وإذاً فأنا أريد بذلك ظهور النتيجة أياً كانت ، نجاحاً أم رسوباً ولا يمكن أن يعتقد عاقل من الناس أن تناقضاً قد وقع بين ماكنت آمره به من الاجتهاد وما أريده اليوم من النتيجة التي تفصح عن واقع أمره .
وهكذا ينبغي أن تعلم ، بأن الإرادة لاتستلزم الأمر ولا الرضا بالشيء المراد . وهذه أيضاً من الزلات التي تاه فيها المعتزلة واضطربت أقوالهم فيها بين كرّ وفر .
فإذا أمعنت في هذا الذي ذكرناه ، أدركت أن الإنسان ، في كل أعماله وتصرفاته الاختيارية إنما يتحرك في دائرة الإرادة الإلهية لا يتخطاها وأدركت أيضاً أنه لا تنافي بين كون الإنسان مختاراً مريداً في تصرفاتـه هـذه وبين كونـه لا يتخطى الإرادة الإلهية ، وليس الأمر كما يظن بعض السطحيين أن فعل الإنسان مادام حاصلا بإرادة الله ، فليس له فيه إذا حرية ولا كسب ، ليس الأمر كذلك إلا إذا صح أن يقول التلميذ الراسب في امتحانه للأستاذ الذي امتحنه : : إنني مقهور على هذا الرسوب ، لأنك قد أردت مني الرسوب عندما أردت امتحاني ، وإلا إذا صح أن يقول الخادم لمخدومه : إنني مقهور على مابدر مني من الخيانة في معاملتك ، تحت سلطان إرادتك التي توجهت إلى اختباري وإطلاق يدي في التصرف بمالك . وبدهي أن أحداً من العقلاء لا يقول هذا الكلام ولا يقبل أن يسمعه
وفي بيان هذه الحقيقة يقول العلامة سعد الدين التفتنازاني على العقائد : ) فإن قيل : بعد تعميم على الله تعالى وإرادته ، الجبر لازم قطعاً ، لأنها إما أن يتعلقا بوجوب الفعل فيجب أو بعدمه فيمتنع ، ولا اختيار مع الـوجـوب والامتناع - قلنا : يعلم ويريد أن العبد يفعله أو يتركــه بــاختياره ، فلا إشكال (1) . فإن قلت ، فهذا الذي تقوله مقنع ومفهوم ، لولا أن في القرآن آية تبطل هذا المعنى الذي تقول ، إذ تدل على أن الإنسان لا يملك لنفسه أي مشيئة إلا بإذن الله ومشيئته ، وهي قوله تعالى ﴿ وَما تَشاؤون إلا أَنْ يَشَاءَ اللهُ إِنَّ اللهَ كانَ عَليماً ﴾
(۱) شرح العقائد النسفية ص ٣٥٤ .
The difference between will and pleasure: Perhaps you will ask after this: How does God punish a human for an act that is among God's wills (murādāt Allāh)?! ... Rather, how can behavior that God forbade to the human be willed (murādan) by God at the same time?! The answer is that this problem stems from a misconception that you should beware of falling into, namely imagining that will (al-irāda) and command (al-amr) are one and the same, and that each one entails the other. This is a great error in estimation. For you have learned previously that nothing occurs in the universe except by His will (irādatihī); otherwise there would be something existing beyond His will and choice, and that is among the clearest manifestations of incapacity and weakness that we declare God Most High to be above. And you have also learned that God says in His Book: 'And He is not pleased (yarḍā) for His servants disbelief, and if you are grateful He is pleased (yarḍahu) for you' [Az-Zumar: 7]. Thus, the disbelief of Abī Jahl, for example, is included among God's wills (murādāt Allāh) as we mentioned, but it is not included in what pleases (yurḍī) God Most High nor in what He commanded, due to the clear indication of the verse. And in the example of the servant that I mentioned to you earlier, there is something to alert you to this truth. We said: You did not intend to let him loose to dispose of your wealth as he wishes, except that you willed (murīd) the appearance of the result whatever the result, whether you love it and are pleased with it or not. This is a truth that we all touch in our experiences and personal actions and our interactions with one another. I certainly do not love that my student be failing in his studies, not successful in it, and I keep repeating to him the command to study and exert effort. Nevertheless, when I want to test him at the end of the year, my will (irādatī) undoubtedly extends to the result that that test will reveal. And so, I will thereby the appearance of the result whatever it is, success or failure. No reasonable person can think that a contradiction has occurred between what I was commanding him of diligence and what I want today of the result that discloses the reality of his situation. Thus you should know that will (al-irāda) does not entail command (al-amr) nor pleasure (ar-riḍā) with the willed thing. This is also among the slips in which the Mu'tazila became lost and their statements became confused therein, going back and forth. So if you ponder what we have mentioned, you will realize that the human, in all his voluntary acts and actions, moves within the circle of divine will (al-irāda al-ilāhiyya) and does not overstep it. And you will also realize that there is no contradiction between the human being being free, willing in these actions and his not overstepping divine will. It is not as some superficial people imagine: that as long as the human act occurs by God's will, then the human has no freedom (ḥurriyya) nor acquisition (kasb) in it. It is not like that, unless it would be valid for the failing student in his exam to say to the teacher who examined him: 'I was compelled (maqhūr) to this failure, because you willed failure for me when you willed to test me.' Or unless it would be valid for the servant to say to his master: 'I was compelled to what emanated from me of betrayal in your dealing, under the authority of your will that was directed to testing me and giving me free rein to dispose of your wealth.' It is obvious that no rational person would say this statement nor accept to hear it. In clarifying this truth, the scholar Sa'd al-Dīn al-Taftazānī says in his commentary on al-'Aqā'id: 'For if it is said: After affirming generality of God's will (irādatihi), compulsion (al-jabr) is necessarily entailed, because it (i.e., the will) either attaches to the obligation of the act, so it is necessary, or to its non-existence, so it is impossible, and there is no choice (ikhtiyār) with necessity and impossibility — we say: He knows and wills that the servant does or leaves it by his choice (bi-ikhtiyārihī), so there is no problem...' If you say: 'This that you say is convincing and understandable, were it not for a verse in the Qur'an that nullifies this meaning that you say, for it indicates that the human possesses no will of his own except by God's permission and will, and that is His saying: 'And you do not will except that God wills; indeed God is all-knowing' — then the answer is already given in the text. (1) Sharḥ al-'Aqā'id al-Nasafiyya, p. 354.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer clarification by Buti on the relationship between divine will (irāda) and human responsibility. It begins with the objection: 'How can God punish humans for actions that He Himself willed?' The objection is based on a misunderstanding — namely, equating divine will with divine command (amr) or divine pleasure (riḍā). Buti explains that these are distinct: God wills everything that happens in the universe, including disbelief, but He does not command it nor is He pleased with it. He cites the Qur'anic verse (39:7) to show that God is not pleased with disbelief. Then he gives two analogies: a master giving a servant free rein but not necessarily liking the outcome, and a teacher testing a student — the teacher wills the test result whatever it is, but earlier had commanded the student to study. These show that will does not entail command or pleasure. Buti then warns that this confusion led the Mu'tazila astray. He concludes that humans act voluntarily within the sphere of divine will, and this does not negate their freedom or acquisition (kasb). To further support, he quotes al-Taftazānī from Sharḥ al-'Aqā'id al-Nasafiyya: Taftazānī addresses the objection that making divine will universal leads to compulsion (jabr). The reply is that God knows and wills that the servant does or leaves an act by his own choice — thus no contradiction. This refutes the claim that human will is negated by divine will, even though the Qur'an states that humans will nothing except as God wills.

Key Terms
الجبر
الاختيار
الكسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That if God wills everything, then humans are compelled and have no real choice (jabr).
Correction: God wills that humans act by their own choice; divine will does not eliminate human agency but rather includes it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does Taftazani resolve the apparent conflict between divine universal will and human choice?
A) He says that divine will only applies to good deeds, not evil ones.
B) He says that humans have absolute free will independent of God.
C) He says that God wills the act as done by the human's own choice.
D) He says that the question is beyond human reason.

Key Takeaway
God's universal will includes and does not negate human free will; the servant acts by his own choice within God's overarching will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you have sinned, have you ever excused yourself by thinking 'it was God's will'? After reading this lesson, can you still claim compulsion? How will you take full responsibility for your choices starting today?
?
You believe God wills that you choose. If that is true, then your disobedience is entirely your own. Do you truly live as if you are morally accountable? What specific habit will you change to reflect that you are not a victim of fate but a free agent before God?
?
The student blamed the teacher for his failure. In what area of your life—faith, relationships, work—are you currently playing the victim and blaming circumstances or even God? Commit today to stop that lie and own your choices as your own.

intermediate
10 min
Human Will Operates Within Divine Will
Buti explains that divine will encompasses human actions without negating human freedom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how divine will encompasses all human actions without contradicting human free will and choice.

Core Idea
Divine will does not negate human freedom; they coexist within a circle of divine will.

This passage from Buti clarifies a critical point in Islamic theology: God's universal will does not imply that humans are compelled in their actions. Many have misunderstood this, leading to either fatalism or denial of divine will. Buti explains the relationship and refutes objections using rational analogies and the authority of Taftazani.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish will from command and approval
Note the initial statement that divine will does not entail command or approval. This is key to avoiding the Mu'tazilite error.
Will (irada) is broader; God may will what He does not command.
2
Understand the circle of divine will
Buti states that all human voluntary actions occur within the circle of divine will, but this does not remove human freedom.
Freedom and divine will are not contradictory.
3
Examine the analogies
The analogies of the failing student and the dishonest servant illustrate that claiming compulsion due to another's will is irrational.
These show that divine will does not excuse personal responsibility.
4
Consider Taftazani's answer
Taftazani resolves the objection that divine will entails compulsion by stating that God knows and wills the servant's own choice.
This preserves both divine will and human choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهكذا ينبغي أن تعلم، بأن الإرادة لاتستلزم الأمر ولا الرضا بالشيء المراد. وهذه أيضاً من الزلات التي تاه فيها المعتزلة واضطربت أقوالهم فيها بين كرّ وفر. فإذا أمعنت في هذا الذي ذكرناه، أدركت أن الإنسان، في كل أعماله وتصرفاته الاختيارية إنما يتحرك في دائرة الإرادة الإلهية لا يتخطاها وأدركت أيضاً أنه لا تنافي بين كون الإنسان مختاراً مريداً في تصرفاته هذه وبين كونه لا يتخطى الإرادة الإلهية، وليس الأمر كما يظن بعض السطحيين أن فعل الإنسان مادام حاصلا بإرادة الله، فليس له فيه إذا حرية ولا كسب، ليس الأمر كذلك إلا إذا صح أن يقول التلميذ الراسب في امتحانه للأستاذ الذي امتحنه: إنني مقهور على هذا الرسوب، لأنك قد أردت مني الرسوب عندما أردت امتحاني، وإلا إذا صح أن يقول الخادم لمخدومه: إنني مقهور على ما بدر مني من الخيانة في معاملتك، تحت سلطان إرادتك التي توجهت إلى اختباري وإطلاق يدي في التصرف بمالك. وبدهي أن أحداً من العقلاء لا يقول هذا الكلام ولا يقبل أن يسمعه. وفي بيان هذه الحقيقة يقول العلامة سعد الدين التفتنازاني على العقائد: ) فإن قيل: بعد تعميم على الله تعالى وإرادته، الجبر لازم قطعاً، لأنها إما أن يتعلقا بوجوب الفعل فيجب أو بعدمه فيمتنع، ولا اختيار مع الوجوب والامتناع - قلنا: يعلم ويريد أن العبد يفعله أو يتركه باختياره، فلا إشكال (1).
And thus it should be known that the will (al-irada) does not entail command (al-amr) nor approval (al-rida) of the thing willed. This is also one of the slips in which the Mu'tazila went astray and their statements became confused between attack and retreat. So if you ponder what we have mentioned, you will realize that man, in all his voluntary actions and behaviors, moves only within the circle of the divine will (al-irada al-ilahiyya) and does not go beyond it, and you will also realize that there is no contradiction between man being free and willing in these actions and between his not going beyond the divine will. And it is not as some superficial people think that since man's action occurs by the will of Allah, therefore he has no freedom or acquisition (kash) in it. It is not so, unless it is valid for the failing student to say to the teacher who examined him: 'I am compelled to this failure because you willed my failure when you willed to examine me'; or unless it is valid for the servant to say to his master: 'I am compelled to the treachery that occurred from me in your dealings, under the authority of your will which was directed to testing me and letting me act freely with your property.' And it is obvious that no rational person says this speech nor accepts to hear it. And in explaining this truth, the scholar Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani says in his commentary on al-Aqa'id: 'If it is said: After making [actions] general to Allah Most High and His will, compulsion (al-jabr) is necessarily entailed, because either it [the will] is connected to the necessity of the act, so it becomes obligatory, or to its non-existence, so it becomes impossible, and there is no choice with obligation and impossibility. We say: He knows and wills that the servant does or leaves it by his own choice; so there is no problem.'
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is an explanation and refutation of the Mu'tazilite misunderstanding regarding the relationship between divine will and human action. The author begins by establishing that the divine will (al-irada) does not necessarily imply divine command (al-amr) or approval (al-rida) of the thing willed. This is a crucial distinction: God may will something that He does not command or approve of, such as the actions of sinful men. The author notes that the Mu'tazila stumbled over this point. He then urges the reader to realize that all human voluntary actions occur within the circle of divine will—no action escapes it—and that this does not negate human free will and choice. There is no contradiction between man being a free chooser and his actions being under God's will. The author refutes the superficial view that if God wills an action, man has no freedom or acquisition (kash) in it. He illustrates with two analogies: a failing student cannot claim compulsion by the teacher's will to examine him, and a dishonest servant cannot blame his master's permission for his treachery. Reasonable people would not accept such excuses. To further clarify, the author quotes Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, who addresses the objection that making all actions dependent on divine will entails compulsion (jabr). The hypothetical objector argues that either God's will necessitates the act (making it obligatory) or prevents it (making it impossible), leaving no choice. Taftazani's answer: God knows and wills that the servant does or omits the act by his own choice—thus the act occurs by human choice within divine will, resolving the apparent problem.

Key Terms
الإرادة الإلهية
الجبر
الاختيار
الكسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God wills an action, humans have no real choice or free will.
Correction: Divine will does not compel; humans choose freely within the scope of God's will. God knows and wills that they choose.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the relationship between divine will and human actions?
A) Divine will necessitates compulsion, so humans are not free.
B) Human actions occur within the circle of divine will but humans still choose freely.
C) Divine will only covers good actions, not sinful ones.
D) Human will is independent of divine will.

Key Takeaway
Divine will does not compel human actions; rather, humans choose freely within the scope of God's will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking that since Allah willed it, you are not to blame? How does this lesson's distinction between divine will and divine command challenge that excuse? What change will you make today to take full responsibility for your choices?
?
The failing student blamed his teacher for his failure. In what area of your life are you currently blaming circumstances or others for your own choices? Will you now stop making excuses and own your actions?
?
If Allah knows and wills everything that happens, does that make you feel helpless or empowered? Based on Taftazani's answer, how can you remind yourself that you are still choosing freely? Commit to one specific choice today that you will make with full awareness of your responsibility.

Understanding Quran 76:30 as Affirming Human Will
Buti answers the objection from Quran 76:30 by showing it affirms divine delegation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti interprets Quran 76:30 as establishing human will as a divine gift rather than negating it.

Core Idea
Quran 76:30 does not deny human will; it reveals its divine source.

Buti anticipates an objection: Quran 76:30 seems to say humans have no will unless God wills. He argues that the verse actually underlies his own explanation, showing that human will is a gift from God. This lesson unpacks that response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the full passage once, noting the objector's claim and Buti's response.
The objector cites Quran 76:30 as evidence against human will.
2
Identify the objector's misinterpretation
Notice that the objector thinks the verse removes human agency entirely.
3
See how Buti reframes the verse
Buti shows the verse as a foundation: human will exists because God willed to grant it.
He calls this capacity 'the great secret'.
4
Reflect on the coexistence of wills
Buti uses his own choice to write as proof that human choice is real yet dependent on divine will.
This shows both wills are compatible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت، فهذا الذي تقوله مقنع ومفهوم، لولا أن في القرآن آية تبطل هذا المعنى الذي تقول، إذ تدل على أن الإنسان لا يملك لنفسه أي مشيئة إلا بإذن الله ومشيئته، وهي قوله تعالى ﴿ وَما تَشاؤون إلا أَنْ يَشَاءَ اللهُ إِنَّ اللهَ كانَ عَليماً حكيماً ﴾ [ الإنسان : ٣٠ ] - فالجواب: أن هذه الآية ليست إلا أساساً ودستوراً للكلام الذي ذكرناه، فهي توضح بصريح العبارة أن الإنسان ماكان ليتمتع بإرادة في كيانه يتجه بسرها إلى اختيار ما يشاء من التصرفات والأعمال، لو لم يشأ الله عز وجل أن يضع في كيانه هذا السر العظيم، وهذا أمر واضح الثبوت، فأنا الآن أختار أن أحبس وقتي على كتابة هذه المباحث الهامة، ولكن أني لي هذا الاختيار القائم على أعظم سر في كياني، لو لم يكن الله عز وجل قد شاء أن يقذف في وجودي، بمحض فضله وكرمه، شيئاً من هذا السر العظيم؟! .. والآن قد أكرمني الله، فشاء أن يجعلني ذا إرادة في تصرفاتي الاختيارية، ألست قد أصبحت إذا مريداً ومختاراً، وأليست أعمالي التي أكسبها ثمرة إرادتي هذه، حتى مع العلم واليقين بأنها دائرة في تلك الإرادة الإلهية ذاتها ؟
If you say: What you said is convincing and understandable, except that there is in the Qur'an a verse that invalidates this meaning you say, for it indicates that man does not possess for himself any will except by the permission of Allah and His will, and it is His saying: 'And you do not will except that Allah wills. Indeed, Allah is ever Knowing and Wise' [al-Insan 76:30]. So the answer: This verse is nothing but a foundation and constitution for the speech we have mentioned. It clarifies in explicit terms that man would not enjoy a will in his being, by whose secret he directs himself to choose whatever he wishes of actions and deeds, had Allah not willed to place in his being this great secret. And this is a clearly established matter. I now choose to devote my time to writing these important discussions, but how can I have this choice, which is based on the greatest secret in my being, had not Allah willed to cast into my existence, by His pure grace and generosity, something of this great secret?! And now Allah has honored me, so He willed to make me possessor of a will in my voluntary actions. Have I not then become willing and choosing? And are not my actions that I acquire the fruit of this my will, even with the knowledge and certainty that they revolve within that same divine will?
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The hypothetical objector (the questioner) acknowledges that the previous explanation is convincing, but raises a specific Qur'anic verse that seems to contradict it: 'And you do not will except that Allah wills' (76:30). The objector claims this verse shows that man has no will unless God wills it, implying that human will is nullified. The author responds by reinterpreting the verse not as a contradiction but as the very foundation of his argument. The verse explicitly shows that human will is a gift from God; man only has will because God willed to place that 'great secret' (al-sirr al-azim) – the faculty of choice – in his being. The author illustrates this with a personal example: he is currently choosing to write these discussions, but that choice itself is only possible because God willed to grant him that capacity. So, paradoxically, the fact that God's will precedes human will does not negate human will; rather, it establishes it. After God has granted him this will, he says: have I not become willing and choosing? And are not my actions the fruit of that will, even while they remain within the circle of divine will? The argument is that the coexistence of the two wills is exactly what the verse teaches.

Key Terms
المشيئة
الإرادة
السر العظيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Quran 76:30 proves that humans have no free will and are merely passive.
Correction: Buti shows the verse actually establishes that human will is a gift from God, making it real within the divine will.

Checkpoint
How does Buti interpret Quran 76:30 ('You do not will unless Allah wills')?
A) It proves that human will is illusory and only God acts.
B) It shows that human will is granted by God and therefore real within divine will.
C) It applies only to prophets, not ordinary people.
D) It means God's will overrides human will, making humans passive.

Key Takeaway
Quran 76:30 does not negate human will; it reveals that God grants humans the capacity to will, so human actions are genuinely chosen yet encompassed by divine will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a choice that leads to sin, do you inwardly attribute it to 'God's decree' to avoid taking ownership? How does Buti's insistence that your will is genuinely yours—granted by God—force you to stop shifting blame and truly repent?
?
If your ability to choose is a gift from God, how does that change your daily gratitude? Do you consciously thank Him for the very capacity to obey or disobey, or do you take it for granted?
?
Think of a moment when you felt your will was powerless—perhaps in a habit you couldn't break. Does Buti's explanation that your will is real and effective (even if dependent on God) give you hope? How can you actively use this gift to seek God's pleasure, knowing your actions are genuinely your own?

Further Quranic Evidence for Human Responsibility
Buti cites three verses affirming human free will and choice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how three Quranic verses (al-Shams 91:7-8, al-Insan 76:2-3, al-Balad 90:8-10) affirm human free will and moral responsibility.

Core Idea
God's gift of will and choice is affirmed by multiple Quranic verses, not isolated ones.

Buti continues his defense of human free will by turning to three additional Quranic verses. These verses make it clear that God created humans with the capacity to choose between good and evil. As you read, notice how each verse emphasizes human agency and accountability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the tone of astonishment and the rhetorical question.
The three verses are presented as challenges to those who deny free will.
2
Identify the three verses
Locate the three Quranic citations: al-Shams 91:7-8, al-Insan 76:2-3, and al-Balad 90:8-10. Notice the keywords in each verse that indicate choice.
Key terms: fujur/taqwa, shakur/kafur, najdayn.
3
Understand the argument
Buti argues that these verses clearly show humans are inspired with both good and evil and are guided to choose between them. This refutes the idea that humans have no choice.
Each verse pairs a divine gift (senses, guidance) with a human response (gratitude/ingratitude, choosing the path).
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that only Quran 76:30 (not cited here) is relevant to free will. Buti shows that many verses affirm human choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووالله، إنه لا ينتهي عجبي ممن يمسك بهذه الآية، ثم يظل يحاول أن ينسف بها أعظم هبة إلهية للإنسان بعد العقل، ألا هبة الإرادة والقدرة على الاختيار! ... وليت شعري ماذا يفعلون، وهم يحاولون هذه المحاولة، بقوله تعالى ﴿ وَنَفْسٍ وَما سَوَّاها فَأَلْهَمَهَا فُجورها وتقواها ﴾ [ الشمس : ۷ - ۸] وبقوله تعالى ﴿ إِنَّا خَلَقْنا الإنسانَ مِنْ نُطْفَةٍ أَمْشاج نَبْتَلِيهِ فَجَعَلْنَاهُ سَمِيعاً بَصيراً ، إِنَّا هَدَيْناهُ السَّبِيلَ إمَّا شاكراً وإمَّا كَفوراً ﴾ [ الإنسان : ۲ - ۳ ] وبقوله تعالى ﴿أَلَمْ نَجْعَل لَّهُ عَيْنَينِ وَلِسَاناً وَشَفَتَينِ وَهَدَيْنَاهُ النَّجْدَينِ ﴾ [ البلد : ٨ - ١٠ ] !
By Allah, my wonder never ceases at those who cling to this verse then keep trying to demolish with it the greatest divine gift to man after the intellect, namely the gift of will and ability to choose! ... I wish I knew what they would do, while they attempt this attempt, with His saying: 'And [by] the soul and He who proportioned it. And inspired it [with discernment of] its wickedness and its righteousness' [al-Shams 91:7-8]; and with His saying: 'Indeed, We created man from a sperm-drop of intermixed [fluids] that we may test him; and We made him hearing and seeing. Indeed, We guided him to the way, whether he be grateful or ungrateful' [al-Insan 76:2-3]; and with His saying: 'Have We not made for him two eyes? And a tongue and two lips? And have shown him the two ways?' [al-Balad 90:8-10]!
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a further argument in defense of human free will and responsibility, using three additional Qur'anic verses. The author expresses astonishment at those who use verse 76:30 to deny human will, because that would undermine the greatest divine gift after reason: the gift of will (al-irada) and capacity for choice (al-qudra ala al-ikhtiyar). He then challenges them to explain how they reconcile their denial with three other clear verses: (1) al-Shams 91:7-8, which states that God inspired the soul with its wickedness (fujur) and righteousness (taqwa), implying that the soul can choose between them. (2) al-Insan 76:2-3, which says God created man, gave him senses, and guided him to the way, so that he may be either grateful or ungrateful—clear evidence of choice. (3) al-Balad 90:8-10, which mentions God's gifts of eyes, tongue, and lips, and then says 'We have shown him the two ways' (al-najdayn), meaning the path of good and evil. These verses collectively affirm that man has the ability to discern and choose, and that he is accountable for his choice. The author's rhetorical question implies that those who deny free will cannot make sense of these verses.

Key Terms

القدرة على الاختيار
الفجور
التقوى
النجدين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only Quran 76:30 is relevant to free will; other verses either do not exist or do not affirm choice.
Correction: Buti cites three additional verses that explicitly affirm human choice and responsibility, showing that the Quran consistently supports free will.

Checkpoint

A) To prove that humans have no control over their actions.
B) To show that God inspires both good and evil, leaving humans to choose.
C) To argue that only God's will matters.
D) To explain that evil comes from God, not humans.

Key Takeaway
Three Quranic verses (al-Shams 91:7-8, al-Insan 76:2-3, al-Balad 90:8-10) affirm that humans have free will and are accountable for their choices.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult moral choice, do you truly believe that God has given you the will to choose good? Or do you secretly blame your circumstances or even Allah for your wrong decisions? This week, commit to making one conscious choice to follow righteousness in a situation where you usually feel helpless, and thank Allah for the ability to choose.
?
Buti describes the gift of will as the greatest after intellect. How often do you thank Allah for the ability to choose? Tonight, in your prayer, specifically express gratitude for this gift and ask Allah to help you use it for what pleases Him.
?
Think of an area of your life where you feel stuck in sin. Do you sometimes think, 'This is just how I am' or 'Allah has decreed this for me'? Read again the verse: 'We guided him to the way, whether grateful or ungrateful.' This means you have a choice. What is one small step you can take today to move from ingratitude to gratitude in that area? Write it down and share it with a trusted friend for accountability.

Proof That God Creates All Human Actions
Al-Buti proves via reason and revelation that God creates all voluntary actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and textual proofs that God creates all voluntary human actions.

Core Idea
Every voluntary action is created by God, without exception.

Al-Buti begins by stating that voluntary actions are among God's creatures. He provides both a rational argument and a Quranic proof to establish this fundamental belief of Ahl al-Sunnah. Let us examine his reasoning and the verse he cites.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Get a feel for the author's flow.
Notice how Al-Buti starts with a clear assertion.
2
Identify the two proofs
The passage contains a rational proof and a textual proof. Find where each begins.
The rational proof starts with 'إذ لو لم يكن...' and the textual proof with 'بالدليل النقلي القاطع...'
3
Understand the rational argument
If any action were not created by God, then God would not possess all attributes of perfection, because something would exist independently of His power. This is impossible.
This argument relies on God being all-perfect and all-powerful.
4
Examine the textual proof
The verse from Al-Furqan (25:2) states that God created everything and determined it precisely. 'Everything' includes actions without doubt.
This verse is a categorical proof (qat'i) for the believer.
5
Note the conclusion
Al-Buti clarifies that this is the position of the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, affirming it as orthodox belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاعلم أولاً، أن أفعال الإنسان الاختيارية من جملة مخلوقات الله عز وجل، هو الذي يخلق فيك الإقبال على الدراسة والانصراف عنها، وهو الذي يخلق فيك تصرفاتك كلها من طاعة وعصيان. ثبت ذلك بالدليل العقلي البين، إذ لو لم يكن شيء من ذلك بخلق الله وقدرته لما اتصف إذاً بكل صفات الكمال ولكان ذلك بتأثير مستقل من غيره، وهو محال على الله، كما قد علمته سابقاً بالدليل النقلي القاطع، وهو قوله عز وجل {وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَقَدَّرَهُ تَقْدِيراً} [الفرقان: 2] والفعل من جملة الأشياء بلا شك، هذا ما عليه عامة أهل السنة والجماعة.
Know first that the voluntary actions of humans are among the creatures of God Almighty. It is He who creates in you the inclination towards study and the turning away from it, and He who creates in you all your actions, whether obedience or disobedience. This is established by clear rational proof: For if none of that were by God's creation and power, then He would not be characterized with all attributes of perfection and that would be due to an independent influence from other than Him, which is impossible for God, as you have already learned from the categorical textual proof, which is His saying, the Mighty and Majestic: {And He created everything and determined it with precise determination} [Al-Furqan: 2]. And the act is among the things without doubt. This is the position of the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a rational and a textual proof that God creates all voluntary human actions. Al-Buti begins by asserting that voluntary actions are included among God's creatures. He gives examples: it is God who creates in you the motivation to study or to turn away, and creates acts of obedience or disobedience. The rational proof is this: if any action were not created by God, then God would not possess all attributes of perfection (since something would exist independently, limiting His power), and that would be impossible. The textual proof is the verse from Surah Al-Furqan (25:2) stating that God created everything and determined it precisely. Since actions are a kind of thing, they are included. Al-Buti notes that this is the creed of mainstream Ahl al-Sunnah.

خلق (creation)
قدرة (power)
صفات الكمال (attributes of perfection)
دليل عقلي (rational proof)
دليل نقلي (textual proof)
آية الفرقان (verse of Al-Furqan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) God would have a partner in creation
B) God would not have all attributes of perfection
C) Human free will would be negated
D) The action would be outside God's power

Key Takeaway
God creates all human voluntary actions; this is proven by reason and revelation, and is the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

When you set an intention to do good, do you genuinely feel that this desire is a gift from Him, or do you take credit for it? What would change in your daily actions if you truly believed that your inclination to obey is as much His creation as the act itself?
?
This teaching implies that no action—good or bad—occurs outside God's will. Does this bring you comfort in knowing that everything is under His control, or does it raise unease about human responsibility? In what specific situation today will you remind yourself that your next choice is created by God, and how will that change your attitude?
?
If God creates both your obedience and your disobedience, then your obedience is not your own achievement and your disobedience is not beyond His power. Where in your life do you feel pride in your good deeds? How can you transform that pride into humble gratitude? And where do you feel hopeless about a sin? How does knowing that God created even that failure invite you to repent sincerely?

Divine Will and Human Free Will
Buti explains how divine will relates to human free will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti reconciles divine will with human free will by distinguishing between God's will to create the power of choice and the resulting voluntary human actions.

Core Idea
God's will creates your freedom; it does not cancel it.

Buti addresses a key question in Islamic theology: if God's will encompasses all things, how can humans be truly free? He begins by distinguishing two categories of creatures: those without choice and human actions based on choice. This passage shows that God's will attaches to creating the very capacity for choice within you, and that this very gift undermines any notion of compulsion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Focus on the distinction Buti makes between the first category of creatures (involuntary) and the second (human actions).
Notice the phrase 'secret of will' – it is key to Buti's argument.
2
Understand the contradiction Buti warns against
Buti argues that if divine will compelled actions, it would contradict God's granting of the power of choice. Identify this contradiction in the text.
The contradiction is between granting freedom and then overriding it.
3
Synthesize the argument
Summarize in your own words how Buti reconciles divine will with human free will. The answer lies in what God's will is attached to – not the action itself but the capacity for choice.
God's will attaches to creating the secret of will, not to compelling specific actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما أن علمه بوجود هذه المخلوقات والأفعال يستلزم تعلق إرادته بها ، فواضح هذا أنه لا إشكال في ذلك بالنسبة للقسم الأول من المخلوقات ، وأما القسم الثاني وهو المخلوقات الاكتسابية القائمة على الاختيار الإنساني فقد علمت مما ذكرناه في المسألة الرابعة ، أن إرادة الله عز وجل متعلقة بخلق سر الإرادة في كيانك ، وهو مستلزم كما تعلم لتعلق الإرادة الإلهية بما تختاره أنت من الشؤون والأفعال بموجب الإرادة التي منحك إياها . ولكن ذلك ليس موجباً لأن تكون مجبراً غير مخير ، وإلا لوقع التناقض بين قولنا : إنه وهبك سر الإرادة التي تنبعث بها إلى اختيار الأفعال ، وقولنا إن ما تختاره بموجبها فعل قسري تقوم به جبراً عنك . وقد فصلنا القول في هذا البحث في شرح المسألة الرابعة التي قبل هذه ، فارجع إليها إن شئت
As for the fact that His knowledge of the existence of these creatures and actions necessitates the attachment of His will to them, it is clear that there is no difficulty in that regarding the first category of creatures. As for the second category, which is the acquired creatures based on human choice, you have known from what we mentioned in the fourth issue that the will of God Almighty is attached to creating the secret of will in your being, and it necessitates, as you know, the attachment of the divine will to what you yourself choose of affairs and actions by virtue of the will that He granted you. But that does not necessitate that you be compelled, not free; otherwise, a contradiction would occur between our saying: He granted you the secret of will by which you proceed to choose actions, and our saying: what you choose by virtue of it is a forced action that you do by compulsion. We have detailed the discussion in this research in the explanation of the fourth issue before this, so refer to it if you wish.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the relationship between divine will and human free will. Buti first notes that God's knowledge of creatures and actions necessarily entails His will being attached to them. He clarifies that this poses no difficulty for the first category of creatures, which are involuntary. For the second category—human actions acquired through choice—God's will is attached to creating the power of choice (the 'secret of will') within the human being. This divine attachment to the creation of free will does not result in compulsion; rather, it establishes the basis for genuine human choice. Buti argues that if God's will were to compel actions, it would contradict the very gift of free will He bestows. He refers the reader to a previous discussion for further detail.

Key Terms
إرادة
اختيار
جبر
سر الإرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's will being attached to human actions means humans are forced to act.
Correction: Buti clarifies that God's will is attached to creating your capacity to choose, not to the specific actions you take. This capacity is what makes your actions voluntary.

Checkpoint

A) God compels all human actions.
B) God creates the power of choice, and humans choose voluntarily.
C) God does not interfere with human actions.
D) Humans create their own actions independently of God.

Key Takeaway
God's will creates the power of choice within humans, and that power is the basis for genuine free will, not compulsion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Rational Possibility of Seeing Allah: An Overview
Introduces the issue of seeing Allah, outlines three aspects, and discusses the first: rational possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the issue of seeing Allah (ru'yat Allah), the three aspects of discussion, and the rational positions of the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunnah regarding its possibility.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah is rationally possible according to Ahl al-Sunnah, not impossible as the Mu'tazila claim.

This passage opens one of the most debated topics in Islamic theology: whether Allah can be seen. The author sets the stage by explaining why this issue is unique—it lacks definitive proofs—and outlines three angles of inquiry. We then dive into the first angle: rational possibility, where we encounter the Mu'tazila’s argument that vision requires a physical body in a direction, and the Sunni response affirming that Allah is not limited by such conditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the three aspects listed at the start.
2
Identify the three aspects
The author lists three aspects of discussion. Find them and understand the focus of each.
Only the first aspect is covered in this passage.
3
Analyze the first aspect
Focus on the Mu'tazila's argument (shubha) and the Ahl al-Sunnah's position. Note the rational basis each side uses.
The Mu'tazila argue that vision requires an object in a direction; Sunnis affirm possibility without those conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعا
رؤية الله تعالى
اعلم أن هذه المسألة مما وقع النزاع فيه بين جمهور المسلمين وبعض الفرق الإسلامية الأخرى ، وسبب ما وقع فيها من النزاع أنها لا ترتبط بأدلة قطعية جازمة مثل بقية مسائل العقيدة ، ولذلك لم يكن الخلاف فيها مستوجباً للكفر والردة ، وإن كانت مخالفة أهل السنة والجماعة - وهم جمهور المسلمين - تستوجب الفسق والجنوح عن الحق .
والكلام يتعلق بهذه المسألة من ثلاثة جوانب :
الجانب الأول : البحث في أن رؤية الله عز وجل مما يجوزه العقل أو يحيله
الجانب الثاني : هل دل السمع ( الأدلة السمعية ) على وقوعها في الآخرة ؟
الجانب الثالث : هل دل السمع على وقوعها أو إمكان وقوعها في الدنيا ؟
أما الجانب الأول : فقد ذهبت المعتزلة إلى أن العقل لا يجيز رؤية العباد مطلقاً ، بل هو قاض باستحالة ذلك . وأجمع جمهور المسلمين وهم أهل السنة والجماعة على أن ذلك مما يدخل في الممكنات ، وأن العقل لا يحيل رؤية العباد لربهم جل جلاله بأعين رؤوسهم
أما شبهة المعتزلة فخلاصتها أن الرؤية إنما هي انطباع صورة المرئي في الحدقة ، ومن شرط ذلك انحصار المرئي في جهة معينة من المكان حتى يمكن اتجاه الحدقة إليه ، ومن المعلوم علم اليقين أن الله تعالى ليس جسماً ولا تحده جهة من الجهات
Fourth: The Vision of Allah the Most High.
Know that this issue is among those in which dispute occurred between the majority of Muslims and some other Islamic sects, and the cause of the dispute that occurred about it is that it is not connected to definitive, conclusive proofs like the rest of the issues of creed. Therefore, disagreement about it does not necessitate kufr (disbelief) and apostasy, even though opposing Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah—who are the majority of Muslims—necessitates fisq (sinfulness) and deviation from the truth.
And the discussion concerns this issue from three aspects:
The first aspect: Investigation of whether the vision of Allah, Mighty and Majestic, is something that the intellect allows or deems impossible.
The second aspect: Did revelation (scriptural evidences) indicate its occurrence in the afterlife?
The third aspect: Did revelation indicate its occurrence or possibility in this world?
As for the first aspect: The Mu'tazila held that the intellect does not permit the vision of Allah by servants at all; rather, it judges its impossibility. And the majority of Muslims—Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah—unanimously agreed that this falls within the realm of possibilities, and that the intellect does not deem impossible the vision of their Lord, Glorious is His Majesty, by the eyes of their heads.
As for the argument of the Mu'tazila, its summary is that vision is merely the impression of the image of the seen object upon the pupil, and a condition of that is that the seen object be confined to a specific direction in space so that the pupil can be directed towards it, and it is known with certain knowledge that Allah the Most High is not a body nor is He confined by any direction.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage introduces the issue of ru'yat Allah (seeing Allah) and presents its first aspect: rational possibility. The author begins by stating that this issue is one of dispute between the majority of Muslims (Ahl al-Sunnah) and some other sects (the Mu'tazila). The reason for dispute is that it is not based on definitive proofs like other creedal matters, so disagreement does not amount to kufr, though opposing Ahl al-Sunnah entails fisq. The author then lists three aspects of the discussion: (1) rational possibility, (2) scriptural evidence for occurrence in the afterlife, (3) scriptural evidence for occurrence or possibility in this world. The passage then focuses on the first aspect. The Mu'tazila argue that the intellect judges vision of Allah to be absolutely impossible. In contrast, Ahl al-Sunnah unanimously affirm it is possible (mumkin) and not rationally impossible. The author then presents the Mu'tazila's argument (shubha): vision requires the impression of the image of the seen object on the pupil, which necessitates that the object be located in a specific direction so the eye can face it. Since Allah is not a body and has no direction, vision is impossible. (The response of Ahl al-Sunnah is not included in this passage but follows later.)

Key Terms
رؤية
المعتزلة
أهل السنة
إمكان
استحالة
شبهة
انطباع صورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that disagreement on this issue leads to kufr (disbelief).
Correction: The author clarifies that disagreement does not necessitate kufr, only fisq (sinfulness) if one opposes Ahl al-Sunnah.

Checkpoint
What is the position of the Mu'tazila regarding the rational possibility of seeing Allah?
A) It is possible if Allah wills
B) The intellect judges it absolutely impossible
C) It will occur only in the afterlife
D) It is possible but not proven

Key Takeaway
The issue of seeing Allah is not based on definitive proofs; rationally, the Mu'tazila deem it impossible while Ahl al-Sunnah affirm its possibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly desire to see Allah in the Hereafter, or has this hope grown cold in your heart? What steps are you taking to ensure that you will be among those granted that vision?
?
The Mu'tazila reject vision because it conflicts with their concept of Allah. Are there aspects of Allah's attributes that you struggle to accept because they don't fit your mental framework? How do you submit your intellect to revelation?
?
This passage says disagreement on this issue does not lead to kufr, only fisq. Does that make you take the issue lightly? Or does it compel you to follow the majority of Muslims with humility, even if your intellect raises doubts?

6 min
Rational Possibility of Seeing Allah
Buti presents the Mu'tazila objection and Sunni proof for rational possibility of seeing Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Sunna refute the Mu'tazila claim that seeing Allah is rationally impossible by redefining the nature of vision.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah is possible because vision is a God-given power, not limited to physical imprinting.

This passage tackles a major theological dispute: is it rationally possible to see Allah? The Mu'tazila argue it is impossible because vision requires direction and physical presence. Ahl al-Sunna respond by redefining vision as a power that Allah can grant in any modality. Let's examine the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author presents the two positions before engaging with the arguments.
2
Identify the two opposing positions
The passage begins by stating the Mu'tazila position and the Ahl al-Sunna consensus. Identify each and note their fundamental disagreement about the rational status of seeing Allah.
The Mu'tazila say 'mustahil' (impossible), Ahl al-Sunna say 'mumkin' (possible).
3
Understand the Mu'tazila's objection (shubha)
The passage explains the Mu'tazila's reasoning: vision is defined as imprinting of an image in the pupil, which requires the seen object to be in a specific direction. Since Allah has no direction, vision is impossible. Grasp this logical chain.
This is the core of the rational objection.
4
Follow the Sunni response
The Sunni response redefines vision more broadly as a power (quwwa) that Allah places in man, not limited to imprinting. The current modality is just one possibility; Allah can connect vision to any modality. Thus, even without direction, seeing Allah is possible.
The proof uses the principle of ontological flexibility: conditions in this world do not necessarily apply to the next.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الجانب الأول : فقد ذهبت المعتزلة إلى أن العقل لا يجيز رؤية العباد مطلقاً ، بل هو قاض باستحالة ذلك . وأجمع جمهور المسلمين وهم أهل السنة والجماعة على أن ذلك مما يدخل في الممكنات ، وأن العقل لا يحيل رؤيـة الـعبـاد لربهم جل جلاله بأعين رؤوسهم . أما شبهة المعتزلة فخلاصتها أن الرؤية إنما هي انطباع صورة المرئي في الحدقة ، ومن شرط ذلك انحصار المرئي في جهة معينة من المكان حتى يمكن اتجاه الحدقة إليه ، ومن المعلوم علم اليقين أن الله تعالى ليس جسماً ولا تحده جهة من الجهات . وأما دليل أهل السنة والجماعة ، فهو أن الرؤية أعم من أن تكون انطباعاً الصورة المرئي في الحدقة على نحو ما يقوله المعتزلة من الشروط التي ينبغي أن تتوفر في الحدقة والشروط التي ينبغي أن تتوفر في الشيء المرئي . وإنما هي قوة يجعلها الله في الإنسان متى شاء وكيف شاء ، يتم بهـا مشـاهـدة صورة المرئي على حقيقته ، والكيفية التي تحصل الرؤية بها اليوم ليست إلا كيفية من كيفيات كثيرة كان الله عز وجل ولا يزال قادراً على ربط حقيقة الرؤية بما شاء منها . وبناء على ذلك نقول : على الرغم من أن الله تعالى ليس جسماً ولا هو متحيز في جهة ما من الجهات ، فإن من الممكن أن ينكشف لعباده انكشاف القمر ليلة البدر كما ورد في الأحاديث الصحيحة وأن يروا ذاته رؤية حقيقية لا شبهة فيها ، وستحصل هذه الرؤية إن شاء الله بدون الشرائط التي لا بد منها للرؤية اليوم ، وكما يقول الجلال الدواني : لا يلزم من كون تلك الشرائط شرطاً في إدراكنا في هذه النشأة كونها شرطاً في النشأة الآخرة.
As for the first aspect: The Mu'tazila held that reason does not permit the servants to see [Allah] at all, rather it judges its impossibility. The majority of Muslims, who are Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a, unanimously agreed that this is among the possible things, and that reason does not deem impossible the servants seeing their Lord, Glory be to Him, with the eyes of their heads. As for the suspicion of the Mu'tazila, its summary is that vision is only the imprinting of the image of the seen object in the pupil, and among its conditions is that the seen object be confined to a specific direction in space so that the pupil can be directed towards it, and it is known with certainty that Allah Almighty is not a body nor is He limited by any direction. As for the proof of Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a, it is that vision is more general than being an imprinting of the image of the seen object in the pupil in the manner of the conditions that the Mu'tazila say must be present in the pupil and the conditions that must be present in the seen thing. Rather, it is a power that Allah places in man whenever He wills and however He wills, by which the image of the seen object is observed in its reality. The modality by which vision occurs today is only one modality among many modalities that Allah Almighty was and still is able to connect the reality of vision to whichever of them He wills. Based on that, we say: Despite the fact that Allah Almighty is not a body nor is He located in any direction, it is possible that He reveals Himself to His servants as the moon is revealed on the night of the full moon, as reported in authentic hadiths, and that they see His Essence (dhat) with a true vision in which there is no ambiguity. This vision will occur, God willing, without the conditions that are necessary for vision today. And as al-Jalal al-Dawani says: 'It is not necessary that those conditions being conditions for our perception in this world entail that they are conditions in the next world.'
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage provides the rational argument (al-janib al-awwal) regarding the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'yat Allah). The author first states the position of the Mu'tazila: reason absolutely forbids seeing Allah and deems it impossible. Then he states the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a: it is rationally possible (mumkin) and reason does not preclude it. He then presents the Mu'tazila's 'shubha' (specious argument): they define vision as the imprinting of an image in the pupil (intiba' surat al-mari'i fi al-hadaqa), which requires the seen object to be located in a specific direction so the eye can face it. Since Allah is not a body and has no direction, vision is impossible. The Sunni response redefines vision more broadly: it is not limited to imprinting but is a power (quwwa) that Allah places in man whenever and however He wills, enabling true perception of the object. The current modality of vision is just one of many possible modalities; Allah can connect the reality of vision to any modality He chooses. Therefore, even though Allah is not a body and not located in a direction, He can still make Himself visible to His servants, like the full moon appearing clearly (as in hadith). This vision will occur in the afterlife without the conditions required for worldly vision. The author quotes al-Jalal al-Dawani: conditions for vision in this world do not necessarily apply to the next world. Thus, the rational objection fails.

أهل السنة والجماعة
إمكان
شبهة
انطباع الصورة
الحدقة
قوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since Allah is not a body and has no location, it is impossible for anyone to see Him in any sense.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna hold that vision does not inherently require location or direction; it is a power that Allah can grant without those conditions.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a, what is the nature of vision that makes it possible to see Allah?
A) Vision is the imprinting of an image in the pupil, but Allah can create that imprint without direction.
B) Vision is a power that Allah places in man, enabling true perception of the object seen, and it is not limited to the current modality.
C) Vision is a metaphorical seeing of Allah's signs, not His essence.
D) Vision is only possible for bodily objects; since Allah is not a body, vision is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Vision is a power from Allah, not limited to physical imprinting; thus, seeing Allah is rationally possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say you believe that seeing Allah is possible. But does your heart truly long for that vision with the same intensity as a traveler longs for home? What has dulled that desire in you, and what will you do today to revive it?
?
The Mu'tazila limited Allah's power by their own reasoning. Where in your daily life do you unconsciously limit what Allah can do based on your own assumptions or experiences? Name one area and commit to praying for His intervention there, trusting He can act beyond your understanding.
?
If the ultimate goal of the believer is to see Allah in the next life, how much time did you spend this week actually thinking about that moment? What change in your priorities would reflect that you truly value this reality?

Mu'tazila Scriptural Proofs Against Seeing Allah
Buti presents the Mu'tazila scriptural proofs against seeing Allah using two Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila scriptural arguments against seeing Allah based on the verses from Surah al-A'raf and Surah al-An'am.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila use Quranic verses to argue that seeing Allah is impossible in both worlds.

This lesson presents the Mu'tazila's scriptural proofs against the possibility of seeing Allah. They cite the story of Moses and the verse 'Vision does not perceive Him' to support their position. Understanding these arguments is essential for grasping the Sunni-Mu'tazila debate on this attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic source passage and its literal translation. Notice how the Mu'tazila construct their argument using two distinct Quranic verses.
Pay attention to the logical structure: first a claim, then evidence, then interpretation.
2
Analyze the first proof: Moses' request
Identify how the Mu'tazila use the verse 'lan tarani' (You will not see Me) and the conditioning on the mountain to argue for the impossibility of vision. Note their interpretation of 'lan' as perpetual negation.
Al-Zamakhshari's role in reinforcing the negation for both worlds is key.
3
Analyze the second proof: 'Vision does not perceive Him'
Examine the verse from Surah al-An'am and understand why the Mu'tazila equate 'idrak' (perception) with 'ru'yah' (vision). How does this verse complement the first argument?
4
Reflect on the Mu'tazila position
Summarize the overall Mu'tazila stance: no scriptural evidence supports seeing Allah, and the Quran itself negates it. Consider how this contrasts with the Sunni view.
This lesson only presents the Mu'tazila side; Sunni refutation comes later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجانب الثاني : وهو البحث عن الأدلة السمعية ، هل فيها ما يدل ؟ فقد ذهب المعتزلة إلى أنه ليس في الأدلة السمعية على رؤية العباد ربهم ما يثبت أن العباد قد يرون ربهم ، بل فيها ما يثبت عدم إمكان رؤيتهم له ، وعمدتهم في ذلك قول الله تعالى حكاية عن موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام : رَبِّ أرني أنظرُ إلَيْكَ ، قالَ لَنْ تَراني ولكن أنظر إلى الجبل فَإِن اسْتَقَرٌ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تراني ، فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَل جَعَلَهُ دَكّاً وَخَرَّ موسى صعقاً ﴾ [ الأعراف : ١٤٣ ] الآية . قالوا : فقد أجاب الله على سؤال موسى الرؤية بقوله : لن تراني - وفيه نفي للرؤية كما هو ظاهر - ثم نفى الرؤية بأسلوب آخر ، وهو أنه علق إمكان الرؤية على استقرار الجبل في مكانه ، وقد علم الله عز وجل أنه لن يستقر دكا ، فقد علق الرؤية على مستحيل في الواقع ، فتكون الرؤية أيضاً مستحيلة . ومن أجل تقوية هذا المعنى وتأكيده ، فسر الزمخشري ( وهو من المعتزلة ( لن بالنفي المؤبد لتتم الدلالة في الآية على أن الرؤية منتفية في الدنيا والآخرة معاً ، ولا نظن أحداً غير الزمخشري فسر لن بالنفي المؤبد
كما استدلوا على نفي الرؤية ، بقوله تعالى : ( لا تُدْركه الأبصارُ وَهُوَ يُدْرك الأبصارَ وَهوَ اللطيف الخبيرُ ﴾ [الأنعام : ۱۰۳ ] قالوا : فقد نفى الله عز وجل أن يدركه أحد بالبصر والإدراك بالبصر هو الرؤية
As for the second aspect: it is the investigation into scriptural evidence: does it contain any indication? The Mu'tazila held that there is nothing in the scriptural evidence about the servants seeing their Lord that proves that the servants may see their Lord; rather, in it there is what proves the impossibility of their seeing Him. Their mainstay in that is the saying of Allah the Exalted, narrating from Moses, peace be upon him: 'My Lord, show me [Yourself] that I may look at You.' He said, 'You will not see Me, but look at the mountain; if it remains firmly in its place, then you will see Me.' So when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain, He made it level, and Moses fell down unconscious. [al-A'raf 7:143] the verse. They said: Allah answered Moses' request for vision with His saying, 'You will not see Me' — and in it is a negation of vision as is apparent — then He negated vision in another way: He conditioned the possibility of vision upon the mountain staying in its place, and Allah Mighty and Majestic knew that it would not stay level, so He conditioned vision upon something impossible in reality; thus vision also becomes impossible. And to strengthen and confirm this meaning, al-Zamakhshari (who is from the Mu'tazila) interpreted 'lan' as perpetual negation, so that the indication in the verse is that vision is negated in this world and the afterlife together. And we do not think anyone other than al-Zamakhshari interpreted 'lan' as perpetual negation.
They also used as evidence for the negation of vision His saying, the Exalted: 'Vision does not perceive Him, and He perceives vision, and He is the Subtle, the Aware' [al-An'am 6:103]. They said: Allah the Exalted negated that anyone perceives Him by sight, and perception by sight is vision.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazila scriptural arguments against seeing Allah. The author first states the Mu'tazila claim: no scriptural evidence proves vision, and indeed there is evidence against it. Their primary proof is the verse from Surah al-A'raf (7:143) about Moses. They argue that Allah replied to Moses' request with 'lan tarani' (you will not see Me), which is an apparent negation. Then Allah further negated vision by conditioning it on the impossible—the mountain staying in place—making vision impossible. The author notes that al-Zamakhshari, a Mu'tazila scholar, interpreted 'lan' as perpetual negation, extending the denial to both worlds. The second proof is the verse 'Vision does not perceive Him' (6:103), which they interpret as a denial of any visual perception of Allah. The passage carefully lays out each argument without yet responding, serving as an exposition of the opposing view.

Key Terms
الرؤية
لن تراني
النفي المؤبد
الزمخشري
لا تدركه الأبصار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'lan' in 'lan tarani' necessarily means perpetual negation (as claimed by al-Zamakhshari and the Mu'tazila).
Correction: In Arabic, 'lan' can indicate temporary negation; the context may not require perpetual negation. Ahl al-Sunna interpret the verse differently, seeing it as a negation specific to this world.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila, how does the verse 'lan tarani' (You will not see Me) serve as evidence against seeing Allah?
A) It shows that Moses never saw Allah
B) It is a clear command not to ask for vision
C) It is a direct negation of vision, and the subsequent conditioning on the impossible confirms the impossibility
D) It indicates that vision is possible only in the afterlife

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila rely on the verses of Moses (7:143) and 'Vision does not perceive Him' (6:103) to argue that seeing Allah is impossible in this world and the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the story of Moses asking to see Allah, do you feel any longing in your own heart to see Him? How does the Mu'tazila argument—that it is impossible—affect that longing?
?
Al-Zamakhshari insisted that 'lan' means perpetual negation, basing it on grammar. Have you ever built a belief on a single interpretation of a verse? What would it take for you to honestly reconsider that interpretation if challenged?
?
The Mu'tazila claim that these verses prove seeing Allah is impossible. If you believe otherwise, what is the foundation of your conviction? Is it rooted in other verses, or in the teachings of the scholars you trust? Are you willing to examine both sides with the same scrutiny?

Scriptural Proofs for Seeing Allah
Buti presents three scriptural proofs and the Companions' consensus for seeing Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna's scriptural evidence for seeing Allah in the Hereafter, including the two Quranic verses and the authentic hadith.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah is established by clear scripture and unanimous consensus.

Ahl al-Sunna affirm that believers will see Allah in Paradise. This lesson presents the key scriptural proofs they cite from the Quran and Sunnah, as well as the consensus of the Companions. These evidences form a core part of Sunni creedal belief about the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Buti lists multiple proofs in sequence.
2
Identify the three proofs
Find the two Quranic verses and the hadith. Note how each proof is introduced with 'famin dhalika' (among that) or 'wa min dhalika' (and among that).
3
Understand the logical connection
The second verse (83:15) is used in reverse: if disbelievers are veiled as punishment, then believers must see as honor. Reflect on this implied logic.
4
Recognize the consensus
Buti mentions that the Companions agreed (ijma') due to the clarity of these proofs. Understand the weight of consensus as a source of evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهب عامة أهل السنة والجماعة إلى أن الرؤية واجبة وثابتة بالسمع ، وقد وردت أدلة سمعية كثيرة تثبت ذلك ، فمن ذلك قول الله عز وجل : وجوه يَوْمَئِذٍ ناضِرَةٌ ، إلى رَبِّها ناظِرَةٌ ﴾ [ القيامة : ۲۲ - ۲۳ ] وقوله عز وجل : كَلَّا إِنَّهُمْ عَنْ رَبِّهِمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ لَمَحْجوبونَ ﴾ [ المطففين : ١٥ ] أي إنهم لا يرونه عقوبة لهم . وهو يدل على أن الصالحين من عباده يرونه إذا إكراماً لهم . ومن ذلك قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في الحديث الصحيح الذي رواه البخاري ( إنكم سترون ربكم كما ترون القمر ليلة البدر ( ومن أجل وضوح هذه الأدلة أجمع عامة الصحابة على وقوع الرؤية في الآخرة
أما قوله تعالى : ﴿ لَنْ تَراني .. ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٤٣ ] الآية . فقد قال أهل السنة والجماعة إنها دليل على وقوع الرؤية لا على العكس كما فهم المعتزلة ، وذلك لسببين :
الأول : أن موسى لم يطلب رؤية الله عز وجل إلا وهو يعلم أنها ممكنة قابلة للوقوع والحصول ، ومن غير الجائز أن يتصور إمكان مثل هذا الأمر وهو مخطئ في تصوره ولو كانت رؤية الله مستحيلة ، لكان سيدنا موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام أولى من المعتزلة بمعرفة ذلك إذ إنّ ذلك هو المتفق مع كمال الأنبياء وعصمتهم وما أكرمهم الله به من علم وإلهام ومعرفة للحقيقة
And the generality of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'ah held that vision is obligatory and established by scripture, and many scriptural proofs have come establishing that. Among that is the saying of Allah, Mighty and Majestic: 'Faces on that Day will be radiant, looking at their Lord' [al-Qiyama 75:22-23], and His saying, Mighty and Majestic: 'No! Indeed, on that Day they will be veiled from their Lord' [al-Mutaffifin 83:15], meaning they do not see Him as a punishment for them. And it indicates that the righteous among His servants see Him as an honor for them. And among that is his saying, peace and blessings be upon him, in the authentic hadith narrated by al-Bukhari: 'You will see your Lord as you see the full moon on the night of the full moon.' And due to the clarity of these proofs, the generality of the Companions agreed upon the occurrence of vision in the afterlife.
As for the saying of the Exalted: 'You will not see Me' [al-A'raf 7:143] the verse, Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'ah said that it is evidence for the occurrence of vision, not the opposite as the Mu'tazila understood. That is for two reasons:
First: Moses did not ask for the vision of Allah, Mighty and Majestic, except while knowing that it is possible, capable of occurring and being attained. And it is not permissible to imagine the possibility of such a matter while being mistaken in his imagination. If seeing Allah were impossible, then our master Moses, peace be upon him, would be more deserving than the Mu'tazila to know that, because that is in accordance with the perfection of the prophets and their infallibility and the knowledge, inspiration, and knowledge of truth with which Allah has honored them.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage presents the Ahl al-Sunna scriptural evidence for seeing Allah and begins their refutation of the Mu'tazila objections. The author first states that Ahl al-Sunna affirm vision as obligatory and established by scripture (sam'). He then lists three proofs: (1) Surah al-Qiyama 75:22-23, which describes faces looking at their Lord; (2) Surah al-Mutaffifin 83:15, which states that the disbelievers are veiled from their Lord, implying the believers see Him; and (3) the authentic hadith from al-Bukhari comparing seeing Allah to seeing the full moon. The author notes that the Companions unanimously agreed on this based on the clear evidence. Then, turning to the Mu'tazila's key verse, 'lan tarani' (You will not see Me), the author argues that it actually supports the occurrence of vision. He gives the first of two reasons: Moses would not have asked for something impossible, and since he was a perfect, infallible prophet, his request proves that vision is possible. The second reason is not included in this window.

The Ahl al-Sunna rely on explicit Quranic verses, authentic hadith, and the consensus of the Companions to affirm that believers will see Allah in the afterlife.

The Mu'tazila Objection and Ahl al-Sunna's First Response
Buti presents the Ahl al-Sunna interpretation of 'lan tarani' and the first reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first reason Ahl al-Sunna give to show that the verse 'lan tarani' actually supports the possibility of vision.

Core Idea
Moses, being an infallible prophet, would not ask for what is impossible.

The Mu'tazila use the verse 'You will not see Me' (al-A'raf 7:143) as their primary evidence against vision. Ahl al-Sunna respond that this verse actually proves the opposite. In this lesson, we examine the first of two reasons: the fact that Prophet Moses himself asked for vision proves that it is possible, for a prophet does not err in such matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that it begins with the Mu'tazila's key verse and then presents the Ahl al-Sunna interpretation.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila argument
The Mu'tazila interpret 'lan tarani' as a perpetual negation, meaning Allah can never be seen. Understand why they consider this a strong proof.
3
Analyze the first reason
Buti argues that Moses would not have asked for something impossible. The fact that he asked shows that vision is possible. Reflect on the role of prophetic infallibility.
The second reason is not included in this lesson, but it will be covered later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهب عامة أهل السنة والجماعة إلى أن الرؤية واجبة وثابتة بالسمع ، وقد وردت أدلة سمعية كثيرة تثبت ذلك ، فمن ذلك قول الله عز وجل : وجوه يَوْمَئِذٍ ناضِرَةٌ ، إلى رَبِّها ناظِرَةٌ ﴾ [ القيامة : ۲۲ - ۲۳ ] وقوله عز وجل : كَلَّا إِنَّهُمْ عَنْ رَبِّهِمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ لَمَحْجوبونَ ﴾ [ المطففين : ١٥ ] أي إنهم لا يرونه عقوبة لهم . وهو يدل على أن الصالحين من عباده يرونه إذا إكراماً لهم . ومن ذلك قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في الحديث الصحيح الذي رواه البخاري ( إنكم سترون ربكم كما ترون القمر ليلة البدر ( ومن أجل وضوح هذه الأدلة أجمع عامة الصحابة على وقوع الرؤية في الآخرة
أما قوله تعالى : ﴿ لَنْ تَراني .. ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٤٣ ] الآية . فقد قال أهل السنة والجماعة إنها دليل على وقوع الرؤية لا على العكس كما فهم المعتزلة ، وذلك لسببين :
الأول : أن موسى لم يطلب رؤية الله عز وجل إلا وهو يعلم أنها ممكنة قابلة للوقوع والحصول ، ومن غير الجائز أن يتصور إمكان مثل هذا الأمر وهو مخطئ في تصوره ولو كانت رؤية الله مستحيلة ، لكان سيدنا موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام أولى من المعتزلة بمعرفة ذلك إذ إنّ ذلك هو المتفق مع كمال الأنبياء وعصمتهم وما أكرمهم الله به من علم وإلهام ومعرفة للحقيقة
And the generality of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'ah held that vision is obligatory and established by scripture, and many scriptural proofs have come establishing that. Among that is the saying of Allah, Mighty and Majestic: 'Faces on that Day will be radiant, looking at their Lord' [al-Qiyama 75:22-23], and His saying, Mighty and Majestic: 'No! Indeed, on that Day they will be veiled from their Lord' [al-Mutaffifin 83:15], meaning they do not see Him as a punishment for them. And it indicates that the righteous among His servants see Him as an honor for them. And among that is his saying, peace and blessings be upon him, in the authentic hadith narrated by al-Bukhari: 'You will see your Lord as you see the full moon on the night of the full moon.' And due to the clarity of these proofs, the generality of the Companions agreed upon the occurrence of vision in the afterlife.
As for the saying of the Exalted: 'You will not see Me' [al-A'raf 7:143] the verse, Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'ah said that it is evidence for the occurrence of vision, not the opposite as the Mu'tazila understood. That is for two reasons:
First: Moses did not ask for the vision of Allah, Mighty and Majestic, except while knowing that it is possible, capable of occurring and being attained. And it is not permissible to imagine the possibility of such a matter while being mistaken in his imagination. If seeing Allah were impossible, then our master Moses, peace be upon him, would be more deserving than the Mu'tazila to know that, because that is in accordance with the perfection of the prophets and their infallibility and the knowledge, inspiration, and knowledge of truth with which Allah has honored them.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage presents the Ahl al-Sunna scriptural evidence for seeing Allah and begins their refutation of the Mu'tazila objections. The author first states that Ahl al-Sunna affirm vision as obligatory and established by scripture (sam'). He then lists three proofs: (1) Surah al-Qiyama 75:22-23, which describes faces looking at their Lord; (2) Surah al-Mutaffifin 83:15, which states that the disbelievers are veiled from their Lord, implying the believers see Him; and (3) the authentic hadith from al-Bukhari comparing seeing Allah to seeing the full moon. The author notes that the Companions unanimously agreed on this based on the clear evidence. Then, turning to the Mu'tazila's key verse, 'lan tarani' (You will not see Me), the author argues that it actually supports the occurrence of vision. He gives the first of two reasons: Moses would not have asked for something impossible, and since he was a perfect, infallible prophet, his request proves that vision is possible. The second reason is not included in this window.

Key Terms
لن تراني
موسى
إمكان
عصمة الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'lan tarani' means Allah can never be seen at all.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna argue that it is evidence for vision because Moses would not have asked for something impossible, and the verse refers to this world, not the Hereafter.

Key Takeaway
The first Ahl al-Sunna response to the Mu'tazila objection is that Prophet Moses' request for vision proves it is possible, as an infallible prophet would not ask for what is impossible.

If you truly believed that seeing Allah in the Hereafter is possible and real, how would it change the way you live this very day? What one specific action will you take to prepare for that moment?
